<span id="freeTextContainer12739651097189813037">Chaos breaks loose when the governor of Virginia orders that speed traps be painted on all streets and highways, and warns that speeders will be caught by monitoring aircraft flying overhead. But the eccentric island of Tangier, fourteen miles off the coast of Virginia in the Chesapeake Bay, responds by declaring war on its own state. Judy Hammer, newly installed as the su</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12739651097189813037">Chaos breaks loose when the governor of Virginia orders that speed traps be painted on all streets and highways, and warns that speeders will be caught by monitoring aircraft flying overhead. But the eccentric island of Tangier, fourteen miles off the coast of Virginia in the Chesapeake Bay, responds by declaring war on its own state. Judy Hammer, newly installed as the superintendent of the Virginia State Police, and Andy Brazil, a state trooper and Hammer's right hand and confidant, find themselves at their wits' end as they try to protect the public from the politicians --- and vice versa --- in this pitch-perfect, darkly comic romp.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18343330850110594092">I would agree... If this were Cornwell's only bad book.<br /><br />She used to be one of my favorite authors, but the entire Andy Brazil series starts out bad and</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18343330850110594092">I would agree... If this were Cornwell's only bad book.<br /><br />She used to be one of my favorite authors, but the entire Andy Brazil series starts out bad and becomes terrible. On top of that, her wonderful Scarpetta series took an unexplained dive from excellent to ridiculous beginning with The Last Precinct. Even her writing style changed suddenly; from first-person, past tense to third-person, present tense (From: "I entered the room and looked around" to "Scapetta enters the room and looks around.") <br /><br />I still highly recommend all the Scarpetta books up to Black Notice.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">No one</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1354230-nanosynergy?shelf=bad-started-discarded" class="actionLinkLite">bad-started-discarded</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1354230-nanosynergy?shelf=mysteries-thrillers-espionage" class="actionLinkLite">mysteries-thrillers-espionage</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1354230-nanosynergy?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1354230-nanosynergy?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer36299737">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17790844681990060998">This is an absolutely terrible book! Cornwell is author of the Kay Scarpetta series (which I highly recommend for readers of this genre - particularly the earlier books in the series). In fact, the Scarpetta books are considered an influence in the development of the fictional, forensic television series (like CSI).<br /><br />However, Isle of Dogs is not part of the Scarpetta series. I couldn't even slog through to the end in audio format. Wincing in embarrassment for the author, I went online to check out</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17790844681990060998">This is an absolutely terrible book! Cornwell is author of the Kay Scarpetta series (which I highly recommend for readers of this genre - particularly the earlier books in the series). In fact, the Scarpetta books are considered an influence in the development of the fictional, forensic television series (like CSI).<br /><br />However, Isle of Dogs is not part of the Scarpetta series. I couldn't even slog through to the end in audio format. Wincing in embarrassment for the author, I went online to check out the reviews of others who had dared to read the entire book. The reviews were overwhelmingly negative (1-star or less). Here are just a few quotes that express my sentiments: - "It's just stupid," "Waste of money," "a truly bad novel." If this was Cornwell's first novel, it would never have been published. If this is a reader's first encounter with Cornwell's writing, sadly it will most likely be their last. <br /><br />The unabridged CD version is 14 hours long (12 CDs; narrator Michele Hall). I made it to the 5th CD, grumbled at my husband about how incredibly bad it was, packed it up and returned it to the library. At least I did not spend any money on this dog. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17790844681990060998">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_97782544">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97782544" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3557180-linda" class="left imgcol" title="Linda"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1307036323p2/3557180.jpg" alt="Linda" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/97782544?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 21, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3557180-linda" class="user" title="Linda">Linda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/392266.Isle_of_Dogs" title="Paperback 9780751531886" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer97782544">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3213778049582675563">This was quite possibly, not only the worst book I have ever read by Patricia Cornwell, but the worst book I have ever read hands down. What a disappointment. I've kept up with the Kay Scarpetta series (which has also been going downhill in the last few books), and thought I'd branch out and read the other series she has written. The Win Garrano series wasn't bad, and was short and sweet (which made it tolerable). However, the Andy Brazil series takes the cake. Hornets Nest (first in the series)</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3213778049582675563">This was quite possibly, not only the worst book I have ever read by Patricia Cornwell, but the worst book I have ever read hands down. What a disappointment. I've kept up with the Kay Scarpetta series (which has also been going downhill in the last few books), and thought I'd branch out and read the other series she has written. The Win Garrano series wasn't bad, and was short and sweet (which made it tolerable). However, the Andy Brazil series takes the cake. Hornets Nest (first in the series) was actually pretty entertaining. But her writing went into a downward spiral with Southern Cross and culminated in her worst novel yet with Isle of Dogs.<br /><br />First of all, one of the main characters, who was present through the first two books, is not mentioned at all in Isle of Dogs. What happened to her? I kept reading, thinking, she'll address this at some point, but about halfway through the book, I realized it wasn't going to happen. Poor form.<br /><br />Second, as a native Virginian (and much surprised, as Cornwell is too), I was appalled by how ignorant Cornwell made the majority of her characters sound. Thanks for making every Virginia resident sound like a bunch of redneck, slack-jawed yokels that can't even tell right from left. I can't speak for Tangerians, as I have never been to the island, but I can't imagine they're as stupid and backwards as she has made them out to be, and believe me, I've heard stories.<br /><br />You should be ashamed of yourself for writing such dreck Patricia Cornwell. How you were able to show your face in public after this disaster baffles me.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3213778049582675563">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1759659195731152571">The story is silly and some what funny and a little scary. The scary part is that I really believe that there are self indulgent politicians with self involved family members, crooked cops and enough stupid people to make this almost a true story. I listened to this as a audio book and am now wishing that there was a way to rated the narration separate from the book. I would rate the book as a 2, but the narrator should be given 4 stars. She did a wonderful job creating separate voices and diale</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1759659195731152571">The story is silly and some what funny and a little scary. The scary part is that I really believe that there are self indulgent politicians with self involved family members, crooked cops and enough stupid people to make this almost a true story. I listened to this as a audio book and am now wishing that there was a way to rated the narration separate from the book. I would rate the book as a 2, but the narrator should be given 4 stars. She did a wonderful job creating separate voices and dialects for the characters. So with mixed feeling I give this audio book a three star rating.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13872496970294209345">I was a die-hard Cornwell fan and even stuck with her when the quality of her writing began to go downhill. Because her early books were so compelling, I kept believing in her long after her gold had turned to dross. However, "Isle of Dogs" was the straw that finally broke the camel's back. It's clear to me that Patricia Cornwell has lost respect for her fans and thinks they'll buy whatever she's selling, no matter how poorly written. Is this what happens when authors start believing their own P</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13872496970294209345">I was a die-hard Cornwell fan and even stuck with her when the quality of her writing began to go downhill. Because her early books were so compelling, I kept believing in her long after her gold had turned to dross. However, "Isle of Dogs" was the straw that finally broke the camel's back. It's clear to me that Patricia Cornwell has lost respect for her fans and thinks they'll buy whatever she's selling, no matter how poorly written. Is this what happens when authors start believing their own PR? I wash my hands of you, Patricia Cornwell.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_13257160">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/13257160" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/819761-marcie-kreter" class="left imgcol" title="Marcie Kreter"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Marcie Kreter" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/13257160?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 23, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/819761-marcie-kreter" class="user" title="Marcie Kreter">Marcie Kreter</a>

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/392266.Isle_of_Dogs" title="Paperback 9780751531886" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer13257160">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16804669846553132347">I only put this book on my list because it was by far the worst book I have ever read. If I could give it negative stars I would. I even wrote to the publisher demanding my money back. Story is horribly unbelievable bordering on plain stupid. It has talking crabs- enough said. I already think Patricia's writing style is questionable and this book only highlighted her weakness. </span>

          </span>

      <a href="/user/show/1768003-sam" class="user" title="Sam">Sam</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/392266.Isle_of_Dogs" title="Paperback 9780751531886" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1768003-sam?shelf=thriller" class="actionLinkLite">thriller</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1768003-sam?shelf=humour" class="actionLinkLite">humour</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1768003-sam?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer157952505">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8255080518377103167">This is the first Patricia Cornwell book I've read and I must admit I was immensely underwhelmed by it. The synopsis on the cover suggested that this would be an intriguing crime thriller with a bit of humour and some quirky characters thrown in for good measure but that's not quite how it worked. Instead the eccentricities of the characters took over the story, which was flimsy at best, and resulted in a poor imitation of a Monty Python sketch. While the story did progress at pace there were ma</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8255080518377103167">This is the first Patricia Cornwell book I've read and I must admit I was immensely underwhelmed by it. The synopsis on the cover suggested that this would be an intriguing crime thriller with a bit of humour and some quirky characters thrown in for good measure but that's not quite how it worked. Instead the eccentricities of the characters took over the story, which was flimsy at best, and resulted in a poor imitation of a Monty Python sketch. While the story did progress at pace there were many moments that just didn't seem to fit and didn't have any apparent purpose. Even having finished it there are still some bits that I really don't understand why they were included. The length of the book is problematic too and partly adds to the feeling of confusion with regard to some of the chapters. There were moments that were rather entertaining though, the Governer is rather amusing and the residents of Tangier are intriguing on many levels. I did also enjoy the entries for Trooper Truth for the most part although these did get a little tiresome by the end. This is not what I expected at all and although it is good in parts the rest is a bit of a non-starter, maybe I just didn't get the humour...</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8255080518377103167">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_39302690">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39302690" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/303465-catten" class="left imgcol" title="Catten"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1226434897p2/303465.jpg" alt="Catten" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/39302690?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 04, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/303465-catten" class="user" title="Catten">Catten</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/392266.Isle_of_Dogs" title="Paperback 9780751531886" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer39302690">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10452548662256556036">If you're looking for a good Kay Scarpetta adventure, skip this book. While the spirited Quincy-like ME appears in this novel, she's just a bit player. Part of the Andy Brazil series, Isle of Dogs turned out, for me anyway, to be a bust. (FYI, Hornet's Nest and Southern Cross were this book's predecessors.)<br /><br />Jumping off from her more serious writing, Cornwell takes a breather, it seems, and penned this odd 400+ page story of pirates, politics, murder, and anthropomorphic* fish, crabs, and dogs.<br /><br />The</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10452548662256556036">If you're looking for a good Kay Scarpetta adventure, skip this book. While the spirited Quincy-like ME appears in this novel, she's just a bit player. Part of the Andy Brazil series, Isle of Dogs turned out, for me anyway, to be a bust. (FYI, Hornet's Nest and Southern Cross were this book's predecessors.)<br /><br />Jumping off from her more serious writing, Cornwell takes a breather, it seems, and penned this odd 400+ page story of pirates, politics, murder, and anthropomorphic* fish, crabs, and dogs.<br /><br />The book starts out with a Dean Koontz flavor. Unique First is 18, beautiful, and deadly. She turns invisible by rearranging her molecules. She is a reincarnated Nazi. She kills people with a box cutter. You can read part of chapter one here.<br /><br />Soon, however, the reader meets Andy Brazil, a handsome state patrol officer who is operating undercover as Trooper Truth, posting essays about the history of Virginia on a Web site that somehow takes the state by storm. Everyone is reading Trooper Truth. The essays are in the book. They deal with mummies, a history of Tangier Island (where the people, descended from pirates, talk "backwards"), cannibalism, spontaneous combustion... Oh yeah, and the end of ever essay has a short paragraph about finding a missing dog, keeping an eye out for bad guys, some actual law-related stuff like that. I failed to see a) why the public would be drooling over the next Trooper Truth posting, and b) what any of it really had to do with crime. It seemed more like a contrived way to have bad guys and good guys communicate using modern technology. (After all, Trooper Truth uses instant messaging!)<br /><br />If you've seen Minority Report, you might be able to relate to this criticism: It seems like Cornwell had a really good foundation for a story, but then couldn't decide if it was supposed to be a comedy, a commentary, a history lesson, or a crime story. It's too much for one book and I really didn't want to finish it, but I did it for you, dear Reader.<br /><br />The character names were even a little annoying - Dr. Faux, a cheating dentist; Major Trader, a treacherous press secretary to the governor; Hooter Shook, a saucy tollbooth operator; Popeye, a hostage female Boston terrier. It's reminiscent of a good Hiaasen book, without the pacing and action.<br /><br />Of course, I'm sure there are some people out there who would like the book, after all it made #14 on Publisher's Weekly's bestsellers list for 2001 (625,202 copies sold - I got mine at the library). </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10452548662256556036">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5242029678965665493">This book begins with Unique First 18 year old malignant demon around for many decades if not centuries. While Isle of Dogs starts with an exciting supernatural-laced attack on a truck driver, it quickly became more like a parlor comedy with multiple subplots. Among the complicated plots: Governor Crimm (almost blind and prone to conspiracy theories as well as suspecting his wife of infidelity) and problems with his aide Trader; Trader plotting against the first female Chief of Police in Virgini</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5242029678965665493">This book begins with Unique First 18 year old malignant demon around for many decades if not centuries. While Isle of Dogs starts with an exciting supernatural-laced attack on a truck driver, it quickly became more like a parlor comedy with multiple subplots. Among the complicated plots: Governor Crimm (almost blind and prone to conspiracy theories as well as suspecting his wife of infidelity) and problems with his aide Trader; Trader plotting against the first female Chief of Police in Virginia; Tangier Isle folk realizing Dr. Faux is a crooked dentist involved in Medicare fraud and they also plot to secede from Virginia; criminals/road pirates aligned with Trader and Unique also against the police chief; a strange relationship between Police Chief Hammer and Andy Brazil (a trooper pilot) and her cute little dog. All of this with Trooper Truth’s blog consisting of historic and other (in)significant posts that also allude to current criminal investigations – such as the search for the dog and a murderer who carved TT on the dead body - and let’s not forget the talking trout and shellfish.<br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1185669373">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1185669373" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10355269-leslie" class="left imgcol" title="Leslie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1340203060p2/10355269.jpg" alt="Leslie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1185669373?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 30, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10355269-leslie" class="user" title="Leslie">Leslie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/392266.Isle_of_Dogs" title="Paperback 9780751531886" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1185669373">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2574748900061239054">I don't generally gravitate to mystery/thriller series -- the plots are too formulaic, the characters too cardboard. I only pick one up occasionally. That's probably why I liked this book better than fans of Ms. Cornwell's Kay Scarpetta series. Though I've never read one of those books, I started "Isle of Dogs," expecting a typical mystery with a strong, hypercompetent protaganist defying danger, deftly solving the crime and perhaps developing a love interest along the way. <br /><br />The book starts out w</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2574748900061239054">I don't generally gravitate to mystery/thriller series -- the plots are too formulaic, the characters too cardboard. I only pick one up occasionally. That's probably why I liked this book better than fans of Ms. Cornwell's Kay Scarpetta series. Though I've never read one of those books, I started "Isle of Dogs," expecting a typical mystery with a strong, hypercompetent protaganist defying danger, deftly solving the crime and perhaps developing a love interest along the way. <br /><br />The book starts out with a really creepy attack by a strange female serial killer named Unique. So then I thought it was going to be a Stephen King-like thriller. But then this parade of increasingly wacky characters is introduced. A blind, impulsive governor and his shop-aholic wife, A manipulative press secretary who moonlights as a pirate. An island community straight out of Forrest Gump. And other assorted ridiculous characters. Throughout the first third of the book I came close to tossing it out several times because the story just wasn't grabbing me. It was too silly and too dumb. But I kept giving it ten more pages and eventually, I picked up on its rhythms. I actually found myself laughing out loud on occasion, such as when Barbie Fogg gives Regina Crimm a makeover. <br /><br />That said, I can't describe this as a successful book. I gave Ms. Cornwell one more start than it deserves just because she tried to do something different. The book has elements of Coen Brothers farce a la Raising Arizona or Fargo. But what it really reminds me of is Terry Pratchett. It's absurdist fantasy. Ms. Cornwell is a deft caricaturist, but she often teetered on the verge of offensive stereotype. The sinister Unique vanished from most of the book because, I suspect, the author couldn't sustain the character. One major flaw in the plot is that all the characters waited breathlessly to read the latest instaillment of "Trooper Truth," an anonymous blog written by the hero. The columns just weren't that interesting! There were many intersecting plot lines, but none were strongly developed. I felt the book came to an end mostly because Ms. Cornwell felt it was time to wrap it up. <br /><br />The book is worth a read, if only as an exercise in thinking about what makes a book good and what makes one awful. <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2574748900061239054">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/565821-rachel" class="user" title="Rachel">Rachel</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer24744930">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1016257262218207037">I agree with many of the reviewers that this was Cornwell's worst book I've read, though I would fall short of calling it horrible. But it was ridiculous, yet not ridiculous enough to be funny. But then it also wasn't serious enough to be taken seriously - it was kind of the worst of both worlds. Even the names in the Andy Brazil series were ridiculous, like "Windy Breezes" and "Virginia West." I guess the part about the island was mildly interesting - that's the best I can say about this book.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_890553612">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/890553612" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/21131599-kerry" class="left imgcol" title="Kerry"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1372602989p2/21131599.jpg" alt="Kerry" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/890553612?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 11, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/21131599-kerry" class="user" title="Kerry">Kerry</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer890553612">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4031147598479040643">If you've read ‘Hornets Nest’ and ‘Southern Cross’, and like me, absolutely loved the relationship between Deputy Chief Virginia West and her young protégée, Andy Brazil, don’t read ‘Isle of Dogs’. <br /><br />In fact, there’s little reason to read ‘Isle of Dogs’ at all, as it’s a complete disaster of a novel. The plot is the thinnest of Cornwell’s books to date, following Brazil, as he explores what can only be described as the adoption of a ‘Gossip Girl’ persona, and Chief of Police, Judy Hammer, fighting</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4031147598479040643">If you've read ‘Hornets Nest’ and ‘Southern Cross’, and like me, absolutely loved the relationship between Deputy Chief Virginia West and her young protégée, Andy Brazil, don’t read ‘Isle of Dogs’. <br /><br />In fact, there’s little reason to read ‘Isle of Dogs’ at all, as it’s a complete disaster of a novel. The plot is the thinnest of Cornwell’s books to date, following Brazil, as he explores what can only be described as the adoption of a ‘Gossip Girl’ persona, and Chief of Police, Judy Hammer, fighting to get her Boston terrier back from a bunch of kidnappers. Yes, this is a book about the kidnapping of a dog.<br /><br />As for my favourite character, the feisty chain-smoking West, she sees a completely unexplained departure altogether. “I don’t know where she is,” is the only account Brazil offers about halfway through the book, and I felt cheated without a sufficient explanation to why such a large part of what made the last two books successful, was completely omitted in this terrible third book. <br /><br />‘Isle of Dogs’ almost compensated with a guest appearance from Cornwell’s key protagonist in her more successful series, Kay Scarpetta, but descended into downright farce with its substories about a visually-impaired governor, a corrupt dentist and a press officer who is descended from pirates. Cornwell clearly showed talent as a writer of comedy in the previous two books, but ‘Isle of Dogs’ struggles to even raise a chuckle. Give it a miss. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4031147598479040643">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer11754024270375965802">The characters were stereotypical and lacking any real depth to bring them to life and the plot was predictable. A true disappointment from a writer who has shown she is capable of much more. I can only imagine she was going through a difficult time in her life and driven by a publisher who pushing for a deadline. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0unqnTTLowGsLE+t832+z58ofBWc4h8jxceu1NFfO4e3PdVOxhm3+yD0OxaNHFh91t+/DNU/WImvzqtGHcrNwg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

But it is art she cannot escape: Oscar has left her his paintings worth millions, and galleries are clamoring to sell them. Just as the early Italian masters painted a wash of vermilion over green to produce the warm flesh tones of their Madonnas - only to have time fade the red to leave a deathlike tint behind - Sigrid begins to see through the vibrant surface of New York\'s art world to the interplay of revenge, greed, and power beneath. These are motives she recognizes from her police work as catalysts for murder. And when a shocking homicide occurs, it hits close to home for Sigrid, implicating Oscar\'s friends and fellow artists in the crime. Her desire to find the killer now puts Sigrid back on the job and out on the street. More than justice is at stake: whether she can still cut it on the force and whether she will ever again dare to love hangs in the balance. Fugitive Colors goes beyond the whodunit genre to combine a top-notch mystery with a portrait of a woman cop indelibly changed - able to notice the background details, the subtle shades, and the <script>
//&lt;![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_104077'), "\n\n  &lt;h2&gt;&lt;a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"http://www.goodreads.com/book/show/104077.Stalker?from_choice=false&amp;amp;from_home_module=false\"&gt;Stalker (Peter Decker/Rina Lazarus, #12)&lt;\/a&gt;&lt;\/h2&gt;\n\n      &lt;div&gt;\n        by &lt;a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/48913.Faye_Kellerman?a=7&amp;amp;origin=related_works\"&gt;Faye Kellerman&lt;\/a&gt;\n      &lt;\/div&gt;\n\n          &lt;div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\"&gt;\n            &lt;span class=\"minirating\"&gt;&lt;span class=\"stars staticStars\"&gt;&lt;span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"&gt;&lt;\/span&gt;&lt;span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"&gt;&lt;\/span&gt;&lt;span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"&gt;&lt;\/span&gt;&lt;span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"&gt;&lt;\/span&gt;&lt;span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"&gt;&lt;\/span&gt;&lt;\/span&gt; 3.82 avg rating &amp;mdash; 2,945 ratings&lt;\/span&gt;            &amp;mdash; published 2000\n          &lt;\/div&gt;\n\n    &lt;div class=\"addBookTipDescription\"&gt;\n      \n&lt;span id=\"freeTextContainer4979804828930656558\"&gt;Faye Kellerman\'s new suspense thriller Stalker is as intelligent about police procedure as it is about family relationships. Cindy Decker is an ambitious young LA policewoman, mistrusted by her colleagues because her father is a senior lieutenant; wh&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText4979804828930656558\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;Faye Kellerman\'s new suspense thriller Stalker is as intelligent about police procedure as it is about family relationships. Cindy Decker is an ambitious young LA policewoman, mistrusted by her colleagues because her father is a senior lieutenant; when someone starts harassing her--following her car, moving things in her apartment--she is aware that it may be no more than a fellow officer with a streak of malice. But coincidences start piling up, connections to the kidnapping and murder of Crayton, a man she knew slightly from the gym, a kidnapping that may have a connection in turn to a series of car-jackings which have progressively escalated into violence against women. Cindy is an attractive flawed heroine--her determination not to go running to her father for help drifts towards foolhardiness and her piecing together of facts from separate ongoing investigations show real comprehension of the teamwork aspect of policing. Faye Kellerman also brings to this excellent thriller a real sense of place--the cliffs where Crayton died become more terrifying each time the plot takes us back there--and a cumulative suspense that comes not only from real jeopardy, but from characters about whom we care deeply. --Roz Kaveney&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a data-text-id=\"4979804828930656558\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent($(this));;     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1025097.Patricia_Cornwell">About Patricia Cornwell</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/1025097.Patricia_Cornwell"><img alt="1025097" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1442522626p2/1025097.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer6308097965266876382">Patricia Cornwell sold her first novel, Postmortem, in 1990 while working as a computer analyst at the Office of the Chief Medical Examiner in Richmond, Virginia. Postmortem, was the first bona fide forensic thriller. It paved the way for an explosion of entertainment featuring in all things forensic across film, television and literature. <br /><br />Postmortem would go on to win the Edgar, Creasey, Anthony,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6308097965266876382">Patricia Cornwell sold her first novel, Postmortem, in 1990 while working as a computer analyst at the Office of the Chief Medical Examiner in Richmond, Virginia. Postmortem, was the first bona fide forensic thriller. It paved the way for an explosion of entertainment featuring in all things forensic across film, television and literature. <br /><br />Postmortem would go on to win the Edgar, Creasey, Anthony, and Macavity awards as well as the French Prix du Roman d’Aventure prize – the first book ever to claim all these distinctions in a single year. To date, Cornwell’s books have sold some 100 million copies in thirty-six languages in over 120 countries. She’s authored twenty-nine New York Times bestsellers.<br /><br />Patricia’s novels center primarily on medical examiner Kay Scarpetta along with her tech-savvy niece Lucy and fellow investigator Pete Marino. Celebrating 25 years, these characters have grown into an international phenomenon, winning Cornwell the Sherlock Award for best detective created by an American author, the Gold Dagger Award, the RBA Thriller Award, and the Medal of Chevalier of the Order of Arts and Letters for her contributions to literary and artistic development. <br /><br />Fox 2000 bought the rights to Kay Scarpetta. Working with producer Liz Friedman, Marvel’s Jessica Jones and fellow Marvel EP and Twilight Saga scribe Melissa Rosenberg to develop the film and find Scarpetta a home on the big screen. <br /><br />After earning her degree in English from Davidson College in 1979, she began working at the Charlotte Observer. <br /><br />Cornwell received widespread attention and praise for her series of articles on prostitution and crime in downtown Charlotte. From the Charlotte Observer, Cornwell moved to a job with the Office of the Chief Medical Examiner of Virginia – a post she would later bestow upon the fictional Kay Scarpetta. <br /><br />When not writing from her Boston home, Patricia tirelessly researches cutting-edge forensic technologies to include in her work. Her interests span outside the literary: Patricia co-founded of the Conservation Scientist Chair at the Harvard University Art Museums. She appears as a forensic consultant on CNN and serves as a member of Harvard-affiliated McLean Hospital’s National Council, where she advocates for psychiatric research. She’s helped fund the ICU at Cornell’s Animal Hospital, the scientific study of a Confederate submarine, the archaeological excavation of Jamestown, and a variety of law enforcement charities. Patricia is also committed to <br />funding scholarships and literacy programs. Her advice to aspiring authors: “Start writing. And don’t take no for an answer.” <br /><br /><br />Social and Digital Outlets<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.patriciacornwell.com" target="_blank">http://www.patriciacornwell.com</a> <br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/patricia.cornwell" target="_blank">https://www.facebook.com/patricia.cor...</a> <br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/1pcornwell" target="_blank">https://twitter.com/1pcornwell</a> <br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="https://instagram.com/1pcornwell/" target="_blank">https://instagram.com/1pcornwell/</a><br /><br /><br />Other areas of expertise &amp; interests<br />Forensics | Forensic Technologies | Ballistics | Weapons | Explosives | Pathology &amp; Autopsies | Crime | Historical and Unsolved Criminal Cases | Jack The Ripper | Helicopter Piloting | Suba Diving | Archaeological Excavation Experience |</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6308097965266876382">...more</a>

    </div>

She brings with her Deputy Chief Virginia West and Andy Brazil, now a full-time police officer. They find a lot of things they are all too familiar with - teenage gangs, a rash of robberies at cash dispensers, street corner drug-dealing, racial tensions, too many people with too many guns and a cardiac inducing lack of parking spaces. They also meet resentment from the established police force and over-high expectations from the city\'s institutions. Then a computer virus crashes the police computer, freezing their screens with a design of blue fish, and the same blue fish appears on the statue of Jefferson Davis, which a graffiti artist has turned into a black basketball player and a gang called the Pikes claim it is their symbol, which also has links to the robberies.
